</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Olifant_Mk2_AAD2014.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Olifant_Mk2_AAD2014.JPG/270px-Olifant_Mk2_AAD2014.JPG" width="270" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Olifant_Mk2_AAD2014.JPG/405px-Olifant_Mk2_AAD2014.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Olifant_Mk2_AAD2014.JPG/540px-Olifant_Mk2_AAD2014.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2248" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Olifant_Mk2_AAD2014.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An Olifant Mk2 tank of the South African Armoured Corps during the Africa Aerospace Expo 2014.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From the early 1990s (after 1992) to 1 April 1997, the SA Army maintained three 'small' <a href="/wiki/Division_(military)" title="Division (military)">divisions</a>, the 7th (HQ <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a>), 8th (HQ Durban) and 9th (HQ Cape Town).<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> They consisted of a reconnaissance battalion, two anti-aircraft defence battalions (AA guns), two battalions of artillery (G-5s and G-6s), a battalion of 127&#160;mm MRLs, an engineer battalion, two battalions of Olifant MBTs, two battalions mounted in Ratel ICVs, and finally two battalions mounted in Buffel APCs. They were all amalgamated into the 7th South African Division on 1 April 1997, and became the 73rd, 74th and 75th Brigades respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 1 April 1997 <a href="/w/index.php?title=Regiment_Louw_Wepener&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Regiment Louw Wepener (page does not exist)">Regiment Louw Wepener</a> (Bethlehem), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Regiment_De_Wet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Regiment De Wet (page does not exist)">Regiment De Wet</a> (Kroonstad) and <a href="/wiki/Regiment_Dan_Pienaar" title="Regiment Dan Pienaar">Regiment Dan Pienaar</a> (Bloemfontein) were absorbed into <a href="/wiki/Regiment_Bloemspruit" title="Regiment Bloemspruit">Regiment Bloemspruit</a>.</p>
<p>7th Division was disbanded on 1 April 1999 and all army battalions were assigned to 'type' formations, in accordance with the recommendations of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=South_African_Defence_Review_1998&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="South African Defence Review 1998 (page does not exist)">South African Defence Review 1998</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7SADiv_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7SADiv-27">[27]</a></sup> The 'type' formation force structure was implemented in accordance with the recommendations of auditing firm <a href="/wiki/Deloitte_and_Touche" class="mw-redirect" title="Deloitte and Touche">Deloitte and Touche</a>, who were contracted to draw up a plan to make the SA Army more economically efficient. The Deloitte and Touche plan had the army separate its combat forces into ‘silo’ style formations for armour, infantry, artillery, and engineers. Deane-Peter Baker of the South African <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Security_Studies" title="Institute for Security Studies">Institute for Security Studies</a> said that the D&amp;T plan, while alleviating, to an extent, the mistrust of the new South African leadership of the remaining apartheid-era <a href="/wiki/South_African_Defence_Force" title="South African Defence Force">South African Defence Force</a> personnel in middle management positions, reduced the combat effectiveness of the Army, and was seen by 2011 as a mistake.<sup id="cite_ref-Baker_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baker-28">[28]</a></sup> Another mistaken decision was the decision to limit the force design of the SANDF to rely on short logistic lines for highly mechanised mobile forces in defence of national territory, as it causes many supply issues during modern foreign deployments. This is one of the major problems of the army and various solutions are being considered by the government to better equip forces deployed in out-of-area force projection operations.<sup id="cite_ref-ISSAF_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISSAF-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>Though non-white personnel did serve as unarmed labourers with the army in both World Wars, a number of non-whites were employed in segregated units during the Border War, and a number of units were completely desegregated, it was not until 1994 – when South Africa achieved full democracy – that the army as a whole was made open to all races. Today the <a href="/wiki/South_African_National_Defence_Force" title="South African National Defence Force">South African National Defence Force</a> (SANDF) has racial quotas to make sure that White, Black, Coloured, and Indian South Africans are proportionately represented in the armed forces.</p>
<p>The post-1994 South African Army has been extensively involved in <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a> operations under <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> and <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> command in other <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">African</a> countries such as the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Mission_in_Sudan" title="United Nations Mission in Sudan">United Nations Mission in Sudan</a> (UNMIS), the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Operation_in_Burundi" title="United Nations Operation in Burundi">United Nations Operation in Burundi</a>(ONUB) and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Organization_Stabilization_Mission_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Organization Stabilization Mission in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">United Nations Organization Stabilization Mission in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> (MONUSCO), and is doing well with these challenges, despite some pitfalls and budget cuts.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FIB-training-01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/FIB-training-01.jpg/270px-FIB-training-01.jpg" width="270" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/FIB-training-01.jpg/405px-FIB-training-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/FIB-training-01.jpg/540px-FIB-training-01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1250" data-file-height="833" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FIB-training-01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
South African soldier serving as part of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Force_Intervention_Brigade" title="United Nations Force Intervention Brigade">United Nations Force Intervention Brigade</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Other operations that the Army was tasked with by government include: Operation Boleas (<a href="/wiki/Lesotho" title="Lesotho">Lesotho</a>), Operation Fibre (<a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>), Operation Triton (five times in the <a href="/wiki/Comoros" title="Comoros">Comoros</a>), Operation Amphibian (<a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a>), Operation Montego (<a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a>), Operation Cordite (<a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>), Operation Teutonic and Operation Bulisa (both in the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>), Operation Pristine (<a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a>), <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_conflict_(2012%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="Central African Republic conflict (2012–present)">Operation Vimbezela</a> (<a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a>) and Operation Bongane (Uganda).<sup id="cite_ref-defenceweb1_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-defenceweb1-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>During 2006 the Army released its ARMY VISION 2020 guidelines document, in a fresh attempt to reassess the 1998 structures which had proved wanting. The army planned a return to a division based structure, from the previous structure where units are simply provided as needed to the two active brigades. In many respects the plan was an attempt to undo the effects of the Deloitte and Touche-inspired force design that came into effect in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-Baker_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baker-28">[28]</a></sup> The new plan was to create two divisions and a special operations brigade to conduct mountain, jungle, airborne and amphibious operations. Specialised training would have had to be carried out, as and when funds become available. A works regiment was also to have been created, to help with the maintenance of army and Defence Force buildings and infrastructure. However the plan was not implemented, and appeared to stall until the issue of the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Defence_Review_2012" title="South African Defence Review 2012">2014 South African Defence Review</a>. With the release of that review in mid-2014 it appears possible that the 2006 planning may be reinvigorated.</p>
<p>The most notable UN deployments since 1994 have been <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_conflict_(2012%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="Central African Republic conflict (2012–present)">Operation Vimbezela</a> (<a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a>) and Operation Mistral, the South African contribution to the United Nations mission to the Democratic Republic of the Congo. The Central African deployment developed rapidly into a combat mission and led to the loss of 15 soldiers from <a href="/wiki/1_Parachute_Battalion" title="1 Parachute Battalion">1 Parachute Battalion</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bangui" title="Bangui">Bangui</a>. The contribution to Ops Mistral, while starting in 2009, became a completely different tasking with the contingent sent in 2013 to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Force_Intervention_Brigade" title="United Nations Force Intervention Brigade">United Nations Force Intervention Brigade</a>, a ~3000-strong intervention brigade that was authorized by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> on 28 March 2013 through United Nations Security Council Resolution 2098. It is the first United Nations peacekeeping unit that has been specifically tasked to carry out offensive operations against armed rebel groups operating in the Eastern <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, specifically those that threaten the State authority and civilian security. They can also carry out their mandate without the help of the <a href="/wiki/Military_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Congolese Army</a>. The brigade is made up of troops from <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malawi" title="Malawi">Malawi</a> and has had several successes against rebel groups such as <a href="/wiki/M23_(militia)" class="mw-redirect" title="M23 (militia)">M23</a> militia.<sup id="cite_ref-defenceweb1_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-defenceweb1-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>All <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a> (SADC) countries, including South Africa, are working on establishing the <a href="/wiki/SADC_Standby_Brigade" class="mw-redirect" title="SADC Standby Brigade">SADC Standby Brigade</a> as an element of the <a href="/wiki/African_Standby_Force" title="African Standby Force">African Standby Force</a>. Working towards the creation and strengthening of these regional brigades should contribute to the peace and security of the region.<sup id="cite_ref-ISSAF_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISSAF-29">[29]</a></sup> The major challenges that the Army face today is to readdress its current force design, to balance its budget, to integrate new equipment to replace several ageing systems, and to prepare forces for the African Standby Force and <a href="/wiki/African_Capacity_for_Immediate_Response_to_Crises" title="African Capacity for Immediate Response to Crises">African Capacity for Immediate Response to Crises</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ISSAF_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISSAF-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_African_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Since the Defence Act of 1912, the South African Army has been comprised, in general terms, of three groupings. The first is the standing army, also known since the 1970s as the Permanent Force. A <a href="/wiki/Military_reserve_force" title="Military reserve force">military reserve force</a> was also established by the terms of the 1912 Act and initially designated the <a href="/wiki/Active_Citizen_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Active Citizen Force">Active Citizen Force</a>. The force was established on 1 July 1913.<sup id="cite_ref-Dorn8_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dorn8-10">[10]</a></sup> Other designations through the years have included Active Reserve Force, Citizen Force, Conventional Reserve and Territorial Reserve.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Deloitte_and_Touche" class="mw-redirect" title="Deloitte and Touche">Deloitte and Touche</a> plan, as well as various policies over the years have referred to a 'One Force Concept' where reservists and reserve units are supposed to be treated on an equal footing with the permanent force counterparts. This is often not the case.</p>
<p>Due to the restructuring of the Reserves, the exact number of reserves is difficult to ascertain. However the 2011/12 planning target was 12 400 reserves.<sup id="cite_ref-AnnReport1112_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnnReport1112-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>The third grouping was initially the Defence Rifle Associations, which later became the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Commando_System" title="South African Commando System">Commandos</a>, a rural self-defence force. There were several thousand other members in the Commandos. Each Commando was responsible for the safeguarding and protection of a specific community (both rural or urban). However, this system was phased out between 2003 and 2008 "because of the role it played in the apartheid era", according to the <a href="/w/index.php?title=South_African_Ministry_of_Safety_and_Security&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="South African Ministry of Safety and Security (page does not exist)">Minister of Safety and Security</a> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Nqakula" title="Charles Nqakula">Charles Nqakula</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> The last commando unit, that at Harrismith in the Free State, was disbanded in March 2008.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/South_African_military_ranks" title="South African military ranks">South African military ranks</a> are derived from that of the British Armed Forces, with Army ranks derived from the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a>.</p>
<p>The SA Army command structure is as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-army.mil.za_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-army.mil.za-33">[33]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/File:SA_Army_structure.jpg" class="image"><img alt="SA Army structure.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/b2/SA_Army_structure.jpg" width="819" height="502" data-file-width="819" data-file-height="502" /></a></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Directorates">Directorates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_African_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Directorates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Chief of the SA Army Force Structure - To structure the SA Army in order to provide the SA Army component of the Landward Defence Capability.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></li>
<li>Chief of the SA Army Force Preparation - Responsible for directing, orchestrating and controlling the combat readiness of SA Army Forces</li>
<li>Chief of the SA Army Corporate Services - Directing corporate resources, services and advice directed towards operationalising the SA Army strategy.</li>
<li>Inspector General - Provides an internal audit service within the Army strategy.</li>
<li>Chief of the SA Army Reserves - To give specialist advice to Chief of the SA Army and his staff in all Reserves related issues</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sergeant_Major_of_the_Army_(South_Africa)" title="Sergeant Major of the Army (South Africa)">Sergeant Major of the Army</a> - To enhance discipline in the SA Army and enforce standards of discipline.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formations_and_units">Formations and units</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_African_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Formations and units">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:642px;"><a href="/wiki/File:South_Africa_Army_2016_Structure.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/South_Africa_Army_2016_Structure.png/640px-South_Africa_Army_2016_Structure.png" width="640" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/South_Africa_Army_2016_Structure.png/960px-South_Africa_Army_2016_Structure.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/South_Africa_Army_2016_Structure.png/1280px-South_Africa_Army_2016_Structure.png 2x" data-file-width="4018" data-file-height="1263" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:South_Africa_Army_2016_Structure.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
OrBat operational units of the South African Army (click to enlarge)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The two standing army brigades are Headquarters <a href="/wiki/43_South_African_Brigade" title="43 South African Brigade">43 South African Brigade</a> and Headquarters <a href="/wiki/46_South_African_Brigade" title="46 South African Brigade">46 South African Brigade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-army.mil.za_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-army.mil.za-33">[33]</a></sup> Each of these two headquarters are organised to provide four headquarters groups. Two of these units should be available for deployment at any one time whilst the other two are on leave and in training.</p>
<p>In accordance with the Deloitte and Touche structure plan, the army was reorganised into single-branch 'formations':</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/South_African_Armoured_Corps" class="mw-redirect" title="South African Armoured Corps">South African Armoured Corps</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/South_African_Army_Infantry_Formation" title="South African Army Infantry Formation">South African Army Infantry Formation</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/South_African_Army_Artillery_Formation" title="South African Army Artillery Formation">South African Army Artillery Formation</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/South_African_Army_Engineer_Formation" title="South African Army Engineer Formation">South African Army Engineer Formation</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/South_African_Army_Air_Defence_Artillery_Formation" title="South African Army Air Defence Artillery Formation">South African Army Air Defence Artillery Formation</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/South_African_Army_Training_Formation" title="South African Army Training Formation">South African Army Training Formation</a></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>- <a href="/w/index.php?title=Army_Combat_Training_Centre_(South_Africa)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Army Combat Training Centre (South Africa) (page does not exist)">Army Combat Training Centre</a> (<a href="/wiki/Lohatla" title="Lohatla">Lohatla</a>)</dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/South_African_Army_Support_Formation" title="South African Army Support Formation">South African Army Support Formation</a></li>
</ul>
<p>Existing and former administrative corps and branches of the South African Army can be seen at <a href="/wiki/South_African_Army_corps_and_branches" title="South African Army corps and branches">South African Army corps and branches</a>.</p>
<p>Many Army units are routinely placed under the nine joint operational-tactical headquarters that the SANDF Chief of Joint Operations supervises directly through <a href="/wiki/Joint_Operations_Division" title="Joint Operations Division">Joint Operations Division</a> (IISS 2013). Brigadier-General <a href="/wiki/Edward_McGill_Alexander" title="Edward McGill Alexander">McGill Alexander</a> took over as General Officer Commanding RJTF South in 2002, but in 2003 he was tasked to close down all the RJTFs.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bases">Bases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_African_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Bases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The South African Army maintains large bases in all 9 provinces of the country, mostly in or around major cities and towns:<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> The army has 10 general support bases, seemingly part of the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Army_Support_Formation" title="South African Army Support Formation">South African Army Support Formation</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_Cape"><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Cape" title="Eastern Cape">Eastern Cape</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_African_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Eastern Cape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Grahamstown" title="Grahamstown">Grahamstown</a> army base houses the 6 South African Infantry Battalion (Air Assault) and the <a href="/wiki/First_City_Regiment" title="First City Regiment">First City Regiment</a> (Air Assault).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Port_Elizabeth" title="Port Elizabeth">Port Elizabeth</a> is home to <a href="/wiki/Prince_Alfred%27s_Guard" title="Prince Alfred's Guard">Prince Alfred's Guard</a> (Air Assault).</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Mthatha" title="Mthatha">Mthatha</a> army base is home to the <a href="/wiki/14_South_African_Infantry_Battalion" title="14 South African Infantry Battalion">14 South African Infantry Battalion</a> (Motorised Infantry).</li>
<li>Greenacres is home to the <a href="/wiki/Regiment_Piet_Retief" title="Regiment Piet Retief">Regiment Piet Retief</a> (Light Infantry).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/East_London,_Eastern_Cape" title="East London, Eastern Cape">East London</a> is home to the <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Volunteer_Rifles" title="Buffalo Volunteer Rifles">Buffalo Volunteer Rifles</a> (Light Infantry).</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Free_State"><a href="/wiki/Free_State_(province)" title="Free State (province)">Free State</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_African_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Free State">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;"><a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Army_Africa_commander_visits_South_Africa_Bloemfontein.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/U.S._Army_Africa_commander_visits_South_Africa_Bloemfontein.jpg/270px-U.S._Army_Africa_commander_visits_South_Africa_Bloemfontein.jpg" width="270" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/U.S._Army_Africa_commander_visits_South_Africa_Bloemfontein.jpg/405px-U.S._Army_Africa_commander_visits_South_Africa_Bloemfontein.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/U.S._Army_Africa_commander_visits_South_Africa_Bloemfontein.jpg/540px-U.S._Army_Africa_commander_visits_South_Africa_Bloemfontein.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3600" data-file-height="2400" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Army_Africa_commander_visits_South_Africa_Bloemfontein.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Maj. Gen. <a href="/wiki/William_B._Garrett_III" title="William B. Garrett III">William B. Garrett III</a> of <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Africa" title="United States Army Africa">United States Army Africa</a> visits the Bloemfontein School of Armour at Tempe Base.</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>One of the largest bases in the country<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> is Tempe Military Base which is located in <a href="/wiki/Bloemfontein" title="Bloemfontein">Bloemfontein</a> and is home to <a href="/wiki/1_South_African_Tank_Regiment" title="1 South African Tank Regiment">1 South African Tank Regiment</a>, <a href="/wiki/1_Special_Service_Battalion" title="1 Special Service Battalion">1 Special Service Battalion</a> (Armoured Car Regiment), the South African School of Armour (which offers decentralized training to regular and reserve regiments), <a href="/wiki/44_Parachute_Regiment" class="mw-redirect" title="44 Parachute Regiment">44 Parachute Regiment</a> and <a href="/wiki/1_South_African_Infantry_Battalion" title="1 South African Infantry Battalion">1 South African Infantry Battalion</a> (Mechanized Infantry). The parachute training wing is also located here. Bloemfontein is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Regiment_Bloemspruit" title="Regiment Bloemspruit">Regiment Bloemspruit</a> (Light Infantry), <a href="/wiki/Vrystaatse_Artillerie_Regiment" title="Vrystaatse Artillerie Regiment">Vrystaatse Artillerie Regiment</a> (Artillery) and <a href="/wiki/Regiment_President_Steyn" title="Regiment President Steyn">Regiment President Steyn</a> (Tank Regiment) as well as 3 Military Hospital.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kroonstad" title="Kroonstad">Kroonstad</a> is home to the <a href="/wiki/School_of_Engineers" class="mw-redirect" title="School of Engineers">School of Engineers</a>, and an Army Band.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bethlehem,_Free_State" title="Bethlehem, Free State">Bethlehem</a> is home to <a href="/w/index.php?title=2_Field_Engineer_Regiment_SAEC&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="2 Field Engineer Regiment SAEC (page does not exist)">2 Field Engineer Regiment SAEC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gauteng"><a href="/wiki/Gauteng" title="Gauteng">Gauteng</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_African_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Gauteng">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li>Army headquarters is located at Dequar Road, Pretoria, which also houses the <a href="/wiki/Transvaalse_Staatsartillerie" title="Transvaalse Staatsartillerie">Transvaalse Staatsartillerie</a> (Artillery) and the <a href="/wiki/Pretoria_Regiment" title="Pretoria Regiment">Pretoria Regiment</a> (Tank Regiment).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pretoria" title="Pretoria">Pretoria</a> is home to a large joint services base called <a href="/wiki/Thaba_Tshwane" title="Thaba Tshwane">Thaba Tshwane</a>, which is also home to the South African Army College, the National Ceremonial Guard and Band, the Military Police School, 1 Military Hospital, 44 Parachute Anti-Aircraft Regiment (Air Defence Artillery), Tshwane Regiment (Motorised Infantry), and <a href="/wiki/18_Light_Regiment" title="18 Light Regiment">18 Light Regiment</a> (airborne mortars). Just south of Thaba Tshwane and within a separate area is Technical Base Complex Centurion, which is home to <a href="/wiki/2_Parachute_Battalion" title="2 Parachute Battalion">2 Parachute Battalion</a>, 44 Parachute Engineers, 1 Military Printing Regiment, 4 Survey and Map Regiment, and the Army Engineer Formation.<sup id="cite_ref-ArmyContact_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ArmyContact-39">[39]</a></sup> Reportedly it also houses the Technical Service Training Centre, and units from the SAMHS and the SAAF. The base, whose TEK appellation may be derived from "Tegnies Basis Werkswinkel", is located at Centurion, south of Pretoria. It has a housing complex for active members.</li>
<li>Wallmannsthal is home to <a href="/wiki/43_SA_Brigade" class="mw-redirect" title="43 SA Brigade">43 SA Brigade</a> Headquarters.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Centurion,_Gauteng" title="Centurion, Gauteng">Centurion</a> is home to <a href="/wiki/3_Parachute_Battalion" title="3 Parachute Battalion">3 Parachute Battalion</a>.</li>
<li>The Joint Support Base in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wonderboom,_Pretoria&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wonderboom, Pretoria (page does not exist)">Wonderboom</a> houses the <a href="/w/index.php?title=School_of_Signals_(South_Africa)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="School of Signals (South Africa) (page does not exist)">School of Signals</a>, 1 Signal Regiment, 2 Signal Regiment, 3 Electronic Workshop, 4 Signal Regiment and 5 Signal Regiment.</li>
<li>Several army bases in <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a> house <a href="/wiki/21_South_African_Infantry_Battalion" title="21 South African Infantry Battalion">21 South African Infantry Battalion</a>, <a href="/wiki/46_South_African_Brigade" title="46 South African Brigade">46 South African Brigade</a> headquarters, 6th Field Engineers Regiment, 1 Construction Regiment, 35th Engineering Supply Regiment, the <a href="/wiki/Rand_Light_Infantry" title="Rand Light Infantry">Rand Light Infantry</a> (Motorised Infantry), The <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg_Regiment" title="Johannesburg Regiment">Johannesburg Regiment</a> (Motorised Infantry), the <a href="/wiki/Transvaal_Scottish_Regiment" title="Transvaal Scottish Regiment">Transvaal Scottish Regiment</a> (Motorised Infantry), Regiment Oos Rand (Motorised Infantry), the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Irish_Regiment" title="South African Irish Regiment">South African Irish Regiment</a> (Motorised Infantry), Regiment President Kruger (Motorised Infantry), the <a href="/wiki/Transvaal_Horse_Artillery" title="Transvaal Horse Artillery">Transvaal Horse Artillery</a> (Artillery) and the <a href="/wiki/Light_Horse_Regiment" title="Light Horse Regiment">Light Horse Regiment</a> (Armoured Car Regiment).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Benoni,_Gauteng" title="Benoni, Gauteng">Benoni</a> is home to Regiment Oos Transvaal (Air Defence Artillery).</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Springs,_Gauteng" title="Springs, Gauteng">Springs</a> is home to 6 Light Anti-Aircraft Regiment (Air Defence Artillery).</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg,_Gauteng" title="Heidelberg, Gauteng">Heidelberg</a> Army Base is home to the SA Army Gymnasium.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Germiston" title="Germiston">Germiston</a> is home to the <a href="/wiki/Witwatersrand_Rifles_Regiment" title="Witwatersrand Rifles Regiment">Witwatersrand Rifles Regiment</a> (Mechanized Infantry).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vereeniging" title="Vereeniging">Vereeniging</a> is home to Regiment Vaal Rivier (Air Defence Artillery).</li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;"><a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Army_Africa_commander_visits_South_Africa_March_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/U.S._Army_Africa_commander_visits_South_Africa_March_2010.jpg/270px-U.S._Army_Africa_commander_visits_South_Africa_March_2010.jpg" width="270" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/U.S._Army_Africa_commander_visits_South_Africa_March_2010.jpg/405px-U.S._Army_Africa_commander_visits_South_Africa_March_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/U.S._Army_Africa_commander_visits_South_Africa_March_2010.jpg/540px-U.S._Army_Africa_commander_visits_South_Africa_March_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3600" data-file-height="2400" /></a>

The South African Army College in Pretoria.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Western_Cape"><a href="/wiki/Western_Cape" title="Western Cape">Western Cape</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_African_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Western Cape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li>Several army bases are located in Cape Town and are home to the 9th South African Infantry Battalion (Seaborne Infantry), The Army Band, the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town_Highlanders_Regiment" title="Cape Town Highlanders Regiment">Cape Town Highlanders Regiment</a> (Mechanized Infantry), <a href="/wiki/Regiment_Westelike_Provinsie" title="Regiment Westelike Provinsie">Regiment Westelike Provinsie</a> (Mechanized Infantry), the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town_Rifles" title="Cape Town Rifles">Cape Town Rifles</a> (Motorised Infantry), <a href="/wiki/Cape_Field_Artillery" title="Cape Field Artillery">Cape Field Artillery</a> (Artillery), <a href="/wiki/Cape_Garrison_Artillery" title="Cape Garrison Artillery">Cape Garrison Artillery</a> (Air Defence Artillery), <a href="/wiki/Regiment_Oranjerivier" title="Regiment Oranjerivier">Regiment Oranjerivier</a> (Armoured Car Regiment) and 3 Field Engineer Regiment.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Oudtshoorn" title="Oudtshoorn">Oudtshoorn</a> army base houses the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Infantry_School" title="South African Infantry School">South African Infantry School</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_Cape"><a href="/wiki/Northern_Cape" title="Northern Cape">Northern Cape</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_African_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Northern Cape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li>An Army base is located in <a href="/wiki/Kimberley,_Northern_Cape" title="Kimberley, Northern Cape">Kimberley</a> which is home to the Air Defence Artillery School, 10 Anti-Aircraft Regiment (Air Defence Artillery), a basic training depot for 3 South African Infantry Battalion, the <a href="/wiki/Kimberley_Regiment" title="Kimberley Regiment">Kimberley Regiment</a> (Motorised Infantry) and 44 Anti-Aircraft Regiment (Air Defence Artillery).</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Lohatla" title="Lohatla">Lohatla</a> training area and army base is home to the SA Army Combat Training Centre where large army field exercises take place. It also houses the 101 Field Workshop and the 16 Maintenance Unit.</li>
<li>An Army base in <a href="/wiki/Upington" title="Upington">Upington</a> is home to 8 South African Infantry Battalion (Mechanized Infantry).</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="North-West"><a href="/wiki/North_West_(South_African_province)" title="North West (South African province)">North-West</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_African_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: North-West">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Potchefstroom" title="Potchefstroom">Potchefstroom</a> army base is home to the School of Artillery, 4 Artillery Regiment (Artillery), Artillery Mobile Regiment (Artillery), the School of Tactical Intelligence, 1 Tactical Intelligence Regiment, <a href="/wiki/Regiment_de_la_Rey" title="Regiment de la Rey">Regiment de la Rey</a> (Mechanized Infantry), <a href="/wiki/Regiment_Potchefstroom_Universiteit" title="Regiment Potchefstroom Universiteit">Regiment Potchefstroom Universiteit</a> (Artillery) and <a href="/wiki/Regiment_Mooirivier" title="Regiment Mooirivier">Regiment Mooirivier</a> (Armoured Car Regiment).</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Mahikeng" title="Mahikeng">Mahikeng</a> Army base is home to 10 South African Infantry Battalion (Motorised Infantry).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Orkney,_North_West" title="Orkney, North West">Orkney</a> is home to <a href="/wiki/Regiment_Skoonspruit" title="Regiment Skoonspruit">Regiment Skoonspruit</a> (Motorised Infantry).</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Zeerust" title="Zeerust">Zeerust</a> Army Base is home to <a href="/wiki/2_South_African_Infantry_Battalion" title="2 South African Infantry Battalion">2 South African Infantry Battalion</a> (Motorised Infantry).<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="KwaZulu-Natal"><a href="/wiki/KwaZulu-Natal" title="KwaZulu-Natal">KwaZulu-Natal</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_African_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: KwaZulu-Natal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Durban" title="Durban">Durban</a> is home to an Army Band, the <a href="/wiki/Durban_Light_Infantry" title="Durban Light Infantry">Durban Light Infantry</a> (Mechanized Infantry), <a href="/wiki/Natal_Field_Artillery" title="Natal Field Artillery">Natal Field Artillery</a> (Artillery), <a href="/wiki/Natal_Mounted_Rifles" title="Natal Mounted Rifles">Natal Mounted Rifles</a> (Tank Regiment), <a href="/wiki/Umvoti_Mounted_Rifles" title="Umvoti Mounted Rifles">Umvoti Mounted Rifles</a> (Armoured Car Regiment), the <a href="/wiki/Durban_Regiment" title="Durban Regiment">Durban Regiment</a> (Motorised Infantry) and the <a href="/wiki/19_Field_Engineer_Regiment_SAEC" class="mw-redirect" title="19 Field Engineer Regiment SAEC">19 Field Engineer Regiment SAEC</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pietermaritzburg" title="Pietermaritzburg">Pietermaritzburg</a> is home to the <a href="/wiki/Natal_Carbineers" title="Natal Carbineers">Natal Carbineers</a> (Motorised Infantry).</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Mtubatuba" title="Mtubatuba">Mtubatuba</a> army base is home to <a href="/wiki/121_South_African_Infantry_Battalion" title="121 South African Infantry Battalion">121 South African Infantry Battalion</a> (Motorised Infantry).</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Ladysmith,_KwaZulu-Natal" title="Ladysmith, KwaZulu-Natal">Ladysmith</a> army base is home to <a href="/wiki/5_South_African_Infantry_Battalion" title="5 South African Infantry Battalion">5 South African Infantry Battalion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></li>
</ul>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;"><a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Army_Africa_Tempe_Base.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/U.S._Army_Africa_Tempe_Base.jpg/270px-U.S._Army_Africa_Tempe_Base.jpg" width="270" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/U.S._Army_Africa_Tempe_Base.jpg/405px-U.S._Army_Africa_Tempe_Base.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/U.S._Army_Africa_Tempe_Base.jpg/540px-U.S._Army_Africa_Tempe_Base.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3600" data-file-height="2400" /></a>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mpumalanga"><a href="/wiki/Mpumalanga" title="Mpumalanga">Mpumalanga</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_African_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Mpumalanga">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Middelburg,_Mpumalanga" title="Middelburg, Mpumalanga">Middelburg</a> Army base is home to <a href="/wiki/4_South_African_Infantry_Battalion" title="4 South African Infantry Battalion">4 South African Infantry Battalion</a> (Motorised Infantry).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Barberton,_Mpumalanga" title="Barberton, Mpumalanga">Barberton</a> is home to <a href="/wiki/Regiment_Botha" title="Regiment Botha">Regiment Botha</a> (Motorised Infantry).</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Limpopo"><a href="/wiki/Limpopo" title="Limpopo">Limpopo</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_African_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Limpopo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Polokwane" title="Polokwane">Polokwane</a> army base is home to an Army Band and <a href="/wiki/Regiment_Christiaan_Beyers" title="Regiment Christiaan Beyers">Regiment Christiaan Beyers</a> (Motorised Infantry).</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Phalaborwa" title="Phalaborwa">Phalaborwa</a> army base is home to <a href="/wiki/7_South_African_Infantry_Battalion" title="7 South African Infantry Battalion">7 South African Infantry Battalion</a> (Motorised Infantry).</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Thohoyandou" title="Thohoyandou">Thohoyandou</a> army base is home to <a href="/wiki/15_South_African_Infantry_Battalion" title="15 South African Infantry Battalion">15 South African Infantry Battalion</a> (Motorised Infantry).</li>
</ul>
<p>The main South African Army Headquarters are located in Salvokop, Pretoria in the Dequar Road Complex along with <a href="/w/index.php?title=102_Field_Workshop_SAOSC&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="102 Field Workshop SAOSC (page does not exist)">102 Field Workshop SAOSC</a>, 17 Maintenance Unit and the South African Military Health Service Military Health Department.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Budget">Budget</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_African_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Budget">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A budget of approximately <a href="/wiki/South_African_Rand" class="mw-redirect" title="South African Rand">Rand</a> 9.98 billion was allocated for fiscal year 2010/2011. In December 2010, it was reported that funding shortages were causing severe problems.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>The vast majority of army equipment is nearing the end of its service life, with some items (like the <a href="/wiki/Olifant_tank" class="mw-redirect" title="Olifant tank">Olifant Main Battle Tank</a>) dating from decades ago.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/South_African_National_Defence_Force" title="South African National Defence Force">South African National Defence Force</a> has however started to remedy the situation with the procurement of 238 <a href="/wiki/Patria_AMV" title="Patria AMV">Patria AMV</a> infantry fighting vehicles under the <i>Hoefyster</i> programme. Other procurements are planned and should follow in line with the guideline document – <i>Army Vision 2020</i>. The SANDF has launched a project called "African Warrior" which is aimed in modernising the equipment and weapons of the SANDF. The project has been very successful in recent years and the South African Army has now put in service a 21st-century <a href="/wiki/R4_assault_rifle" class="mw-redirect" title="R4 assault rifle">R4 assault rifle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Equipment">Equipment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_African_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Equipment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Equipment_of_the_South_African_Army" title="Equipment of the South African Army">Equipment of the South African Army</a></div>
<p>The South African Army maintains a wide variety of military equipment.</p>
